# Coockiemonster
Coockiemonster.md

ArticlePage-hero-container-1BcoN"><div class="TwoColumnsLayout-inner-e5KaJ"><div dir="ltr" class="ArticlePage-article-header-23J2O"><div class="ArticleHeader-info-container-3-6YG"><a class="TextLabel__text-label___3oCVw TextLabel__black-to-orange___23uc0 TextLabel__small-all-caps___2Z2RG ArticleHeader-channel-1DzNK" href="https://www.reuters.com/news/archive/BigStory11">Commodities News</a><div class="ArticleHeader-date-line-3oc3Y"><time class="TextLabel__text-label___3oCVw TextLabel__gray___1V4fk TextLabel__small-all-caps___2Z2RG ArticleHeader-date-Goy3y"></time><time class="TextLabel__text-label___3oCVw TextLabel__gray___1V4fk TextLabel__small-all-caps___2Z2RG ArticleHeader-date-Goy3y"></time><time class="TextLabel__text-label___3oCVw TextLabel__gray___1V4fk TextLabel__small-all-caps___2Z2RG ArticleHeader-date-Goy3y">Updated </time></div></div><h1 class="Headline-headline-2FXIq Headline-black-OogpV ArticleHeader-headline-NlAqj">Exclusive: Arrival of Putin&#x27;s judo partner squeezed Shell out of LNG project - sources</h1></div></div></div></div><div class="TwoColumnsLayout-body-86gsE ArticlePage-body-container-10RhS"><div class="TwoColumnsLayout-left-column-CYquM"><article dir="ltr" class="ArticlePage-article-body-1xN5M"><div class="ArticleBodyWrapper"><div class="ArticleBody-byline-container-3H6dy"><p class="Byline-byline-1sVmo ArticleBody-byline-10B7D">By <a class="TextLabel__text-label___3oCVw TextLabel__black-to-orange___23uc0 TextLabel__serif___3lOpX Byline-author-2BSir" href="https://www.reuters.com/journalists/dmitry-zhdannikov" target="_blank">Dmitry Zhdannikov</a>, <a class="TextLabel__text-label___3oCVw TextLabel__black-to-orange___23uc0 TextLabel__serif___3lOpX Byline-author-2BSir" href="https://www.reuters.com/journalists/olesya-astakhova" target="_blank">Olesya Astakhova</a></p><div class="ArticleBody-read-time-and-social-2VOIr"><p class="TextLabel__text-label___3oCVw TextLabel__gray___1V4fk TextLabel__small-all-caps-spaced-out___3O9H4 ReadTime-read-time-1s3CG ArticleBody-read-time-29pGN">5 Min Read</p><div class="SocialTools__container___3rfoZ"><button aria-label="Facebook" type="button" class="SocialTools__icon___MYRE6 SocialTools__facebook___3tojW SocialTools__gray-to-original___1Duya"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 9 16"><path d="M5.8 16V8.7h2.7l.4-2.8H5.8V4c0-.8.2-1.4 1.5-1.4H9V.1C8.7.1 7.8 0 6.6 0c-2.3 0-4 1.3-4 3.8v2.1H0v2.8h2.7V16h3.1z"></path></svg></button><button aria-label="Twitter" type="button" class="SocialTools__icon___MYRE6 SocialTools__twitter___1EoE2 SocialTools__gray-to-original___1Duya"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 512 512"><path d="M512.002 97.211c-18.84 8.354-39.082 14.001-60.33 16.54 21.686-13 38.342-33.585 46.186-58.115a210.29 210.29 0 0 1-66.705 25.49c-19.16-20.415-46.461-33.17-76.674-33.17-58.011 0-105.042 47.029-105.042 105.039 0 8.233.929 16.25 2.72 23.939-87.3-4.382-164.701-46.2-216.509-109.753-9.042 15.514-14.223 33.558-14.223 52.809 0 36.444 18.544 68.596 46.73 87.433a104.614 104.614 0 0 1-47.577-13.139c-.01.438-.01.878-.01 1.321 0 50.894 36.209 93.348 84.261 103a105.245 105.245 0 0 1-27.674 3.687c-6.769 0-13.349-.66-19.764-1.888 13.368 41.73 52.16 72.104 98.126 72.949-35.95 28.176-81.243 44.967-130.458 44.967-8.479 0-16.84-.496-25.058-1.471 46.486 29.807 101.701 47.197 161.021 47.197 193.211 0 298.868-160.062 298.868-298.872 0-4.554-.104-9.084-.305-13.59 20.526-14.809 38.335-33.309 52.417-54.373z"></path></svg></button></div></div></div><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">LONDON/MOSCOW (Reuters) - Royal Dutch Shell pulled out of a project to build a Russian liquefied natural gas plant partly because Gazprom suddenly added another partner with links to an ally of President Vladimir Putin, according to five sources.</p><figure class="WithCaption-container-Aau3d WithCaption-outside-2Jvzs"><div><button type="button" class="FullscreenOverlay-button-1FTU6 Slideshow-inline-image-container-1dktB" aria-label="image"><figure><div class="Slideshow-inline-image-1uoB6"><div class="BackdropImage-container-2S9Qf" style="height:0;padding-bottom:65.88%"><div class="BackdropImage-backdrop-14yhl AutoSizeImage-container-19DRs" role="img" aria-label="FILE PHOTO: The logo of Gazprom marketing department is seen in front of the office located on the Champs Elysees in Paris ,January 5, 2009. REUTERS/Charles Platiau" title="FILE PHOTO: The logo of Gazprom marketing department is seen in front of the office located on the Champs Elysees in Paris ,January 5, 2009. REUTERS/Charles Platiau"></div><div class="BackdropImage-image-a7Ah5 AutoSizeImage-container-19DRs" role="img" aria-label="FILE PHOTO: The logo of Gazprom marketing department is seen in front of the office located on the Champs Elysees in Paris ,January 5, 2009. REUTERS/Charles Platiau" title="FILE PHOTO: The logo of Gazprom marketing department is seen in front of the office located on the Champs Elysees in Paris ,January 5, 2009. REUTERS/Charles Platiau"></div></div></div><div class="Slideshow-expand-button-2c_q7"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 18 18"><path d="M16.293 1H12.5a.5.5 0 1 1 0-1h5a.5.5 0 0 1 .5.5v5a.5.5 0 1 1-1 0V1.707l-4.146 4.147a.5.5 0 0 1-.708-.708L16.293 1zM1 16.293l4.146-4.147a.5.5 0 0 1 .708.708L1.707 17H5.5a.5.5 0 1 1 0 1h-5a.5.5 0 0 1-.5-.5v-5a.5.5 0 1 1 1 0v3.793z"></path></svg></div></figure></button></div><div class="WithCaption-caption-container-Y-li-"><figcaption>FILE PHOTO: The logo of Gazprom marketing department is seen in front of the office located on the Champs Elysees in Paris ,January 5, 2009. REUTERS/Charles Platiau</figcaption></div></figure><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">After three years work on the Baltic Coast project, Shell discovered that Gazprom was bringing in a company linked to Arkady Rotenberg, who is on a U.S. sanctions blacklist.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">The sudden change in the line-up of partners was one of the key factors contributing to Shell’s Wednesday announcement that it was pulling out of the project, according to three sources close to Shell and two other sources familiar with the project.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">Asked to comment on the reasons for withdrawing, a Shell spokesman said it had nothing to add to a previous statement that said its exit followed Gazprom’s announcement last month of its final concept for the project. Gazprom spokesman Sergei Kupriyanov said the company was not commenting.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">According to the two sources close to Shell, Gazprom did not consult with Shell about bringing in the firm, which is called RusGazDobycha, but instead presented it with the plan as a fait accompli.</p><div class="AdSlot__container___2BqUD ArticleBody-ad-slot-83sCj"><div class="AdSlot__creative___aEugP" id="ad_mpu"></div></div><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">With RusGazDobycha’s arrival also came changes to the configuration of the project itself, which Shell did not feel comfortable with, all of the sources said.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">It became untenable for Shell to stay in the project “and that was clear from the moment that Gazprom announced it was going to build the plant together with RusGazDobycha,” said one of the sources familiar with the project.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">A RusGazDobycha official did not respond to a request for comment. Asked if the presidential administration had any role in RusGazDobycha’s entry into the project, Kremlin spokesman Dmitry Peskov said it was a question for the companies involved.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">The sudden shift in the project underlines the unpredictability of doing business in Russia -- even for a firm like Shell with a long pedigree of successful cooperation. It also shows how Rotenberg’s business empire, focused mainly on construction and engineering, is expanding into the energy sector.</p><div class="ArticleBody-inline-image-small-3wN0R"><button type="button" class="FullscreenOverlay-button-1FTU6 Slideshow-inline-image-container-1dktB" aria-label="image"><figure><div class="Slideshow-inline-image-1uoB6"><div class="BackdropImage-container-2S9Qf" style="height:0;padding-bottom:65.88%"><div class="BackdropImage-backdrop-14yhl AutoSizeImage-container-19DRs" role="img" aria-label="FILE PHOTO: A Shell logo is seen on fuel pump while a car is refueled at in Warsaw, Poland, June 1, 2017. REUTERS/Kacper Pempel" title="FILE PHOTO: A Shell logo is seen on fuel pump while a car is refueled at in Warsaw, Poland, June 1, 2017. REUTERS/Kacper Pempel"></div><div class="BackdropImage-image-a7Ah5 AutoSizeImage-container-19DRs" role="img" aria-label="FILE PHOTO: A Shell logo is seen on fuel pump while a car is refueled at in Warsaw, Poland, June 1, 2017. REUTERS/Kacper Pempel" title="FILE PHOTO: A Shell logo is seen on fuel pump while a car is refueled at in Warsaw, Poland, June 1, 2017. REUTERS/Kacper Pempel"></div></div></div><div class="Slideshow-expand-button-2c_q7"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 18 18"><path d="M16.293 1H12.5a.5.5 0 1 1 0-1h5a.5.5 0 0 1 .5.5v5a.5.5 0 1 1-1 0V1.707l-4.146 4.147a.5.5 0 0 1-.708-.708L16.293 1zM1 16.293l4.146-4.147a.5.5 0 0 1 .708.708L1.707 17H5.5a.5.5 0 1 1 0 1h-5a.5.5 0 0 1-.5-.5v-5a.5.5 0 1 1 1 0v3.793z"></path></svg></div></figure></button></div><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">Shell said that its other joint projects in Russia -- chief among them the Gazprom-led Sakhalin-2 LNG plant -- would be unaffected by its exit from the Baltic LNG project.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">But Shell’s involvement in Sakhalin expires this month. Unless the Russian government decides to extend the Sakhalin deal, Shell’s portfolio of Russian projects will be left looking thin.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">The Russian government has given no indication as to whether it would extend Shell’s Sakhalin contract.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">“DIGGING YOUR OWN GRAVE”</p><div class="AdSlot__container___2BqUD ArticleBody-ad-slot-83sCj"><div class="AdSlot__creative___aEugP" id="mpu_native"></div></div><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">One of the problems for Shell was that Rotenberg, a long-standing friend of Putin and his former judo training partner, was under sanctions and that created sanctions risks for Shell too, according to one of the sources close to Shell and the second source familiar with the project.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">For Shell, partnering with a Rotenberg-linked firm was tantamount to “digging yourself your own sanctions grave,” said that source.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">But the other sources said the primary issue for Shell was the change in the configuration of the LNG project.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">RusGazDobycha is 100 percent-owned by a firm called National Gas Group (NGG), according to the Spark database, which collates official data from the tax agency and the state statistics agency.</p><div class="AdSlot__container___2BqUD ArticleBody-ad-slot-83sCj"><div class="AdSlot__creative___aEugP" id="mpu_lower"></div></div><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">Until November 2016, Rotenberg had a 51 percent stake in NGG, the database shows. The majority owner of NGG now is Artyom Obolensky, who is also chairman of the board of SMP Bank, controlled by Arkady Rotenberg and his brother Boris.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">A representative of Arkady Rotenberg, asked about the Baltic LNG project, said Rotenberg “has no interests in this business.”</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">The brothers were both added to the U.S. Treasury Department’s sanctions blacklist in March 2014.</p><p class="Paragraph-paragraph-2Bgue ArticleBody-para-TD_9x">The sanctions designation stated that the brothers had amassed enormous amounts of wealth during the years of Putin’s rule, and that they had received high-price contracts to carry out work for Gazprom and the 2014 Winter Olympic games in the Russian Black Sea resort of Sochi.</p><div><div class="Attribution-attribution-Y5JpY"><p>Additional reporting by Maria Grabar, Vladimir Soldatkin Gleb Stolyarov and Polina Nikolskaya; Writing by Christian Lowe; Editing by Anna Willard</p></div><div class="TrustBadge-trust-badge-20GM8"><p>Our Standards: <a href="http://thomsonreuters.com/en/about-us/trust-principles.html">The Thomson Reuters Trust Principles.</a></p></div></div></div></article></div><div REUTERS/Kacper Pempel"}],"has_dianomi_unit":true,"has_logly_unit":false,"layout":{"type":"default","body":"default"},"primary_asset_type":"slideshow","body_items":[{"type":"paragraph","content":"LONDON/MOSCOW (Reuters) - Royal Dutch Shell pulled out of a project to build a Russian liquefied natural gas plant partly because Gazprom suddenly added another partner with links to an ally of President Vladimir Putin, according to five sources."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"After three years work on the Baltic Coast project, Shell discovered that Gazprom was bringing in a company linked to Arkady Rotenberg, who is on a U.S. sanctions blacklist."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"The sudden change in the line-up of partners was one of the key factors contributing to Shell’s Wednesday announcement that it was pulling out of the project, according to three sources close to Shell and two other sources familiar with the project."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"Asked to comment on the reasons for withdrawing, a Shell spokesman said it had nothing to add to a previous statement that said its exit followed Gazprom’s announcement last month of its final concept for the project. Gazprom spokesman Sergei Kupriyanov said the company was not commenting."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"According to the two sources close to Shell, Gazprom did not consult with Shell about bringing in the firm, which is called RusGazDobycha, but instead presented it with the plan as a fait accompli."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"With RusGazDobycha’s arrival also came changes to the configuration of the project itself, which Shell did not feel comfortable with, all of the sources said."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"It became untenable for Shell to stay in the project “and that was clear from the moment that Gazprom announced it was going to build the plant together with RusGazDobycha,” said one of the sources familiar with the project."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"A RusGazDobycha official did not respond to a request for comment. Asked if the presidential administration had any role in RusGazDobycha’s entry into the project, Kremlin spokesman Dmitry Peskov said it was a question for the companies involved."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"The sudden shift in the project underlines the unpredictability of doing business in Russia -- even for a firm like Shell with a long pedigree of successful cooperation. It also shows how Rotenberg’s business empire, focused mainly on construction and engineering, is expanding into the energy sector."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"Shell said that its other joint projects in Russia -- chief among them the Gazprom-led Sakhalin-2 LNG plant -- would be unaffected by its exit from the Baltic LNG project."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"But Shell’s involvement in Sakhalin expires this month. Unless the Russian government decides to extend the Sakhalin deal, Shell’s portfolio of Russian projects will be left looking thin."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"The Russian government has given no indication as to whether it would extend Shell’s Sakhalin contract."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"“DIGGING YOUR OWN GRAVE”"},{"type":"paragraph","content":"One of the problems for Shell was that Rotenberg, a long-standing friend of Putin and his former judo training partner, was under sanctions and that created sanctions risks for Shell too, according to one of the sources close to Shell and the second source familiar with the project."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"For Shell, partnering with a Rotenberg-linked firm was tantamount to “digging yourself your own sanctions grave,” said that source."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"But the other sources said the primary issue for Shell was the change in the configuration of the LNG project."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"RusGazDobycha is 100 percent-owned by a firm called National Gas Group (NGG), according to the Spark database, which collates official data from the tax agency and the state statistics agency."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"Until November 2016, Rotenberg had a 51 percent stake in NGG, the database shows. The majority owner of NGG now is Artyom Obolensky, who is also chairman of the board of SMP Bank, controlled by Arkady Rotenberg and his brother Boris."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"A representative of Arkady Rotenberg, asked about the Baltic LNG project, said Rotenberg “has no interests in this business.”"},{"type":"paragraph","content":"The brothers were both added to the U.S. Treasury Department’s sanctions blacklist in March 2014."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"The sanctions designation stated that the brothers had amassed enormous amounts of wealth during the years of Putin’s rule, and that they had received high-price contracts to carry out work for Gazprom and the 2014 Winter Olympic games in the Russian Black Sea resort of Sochi."}],"body_items_shaped":[{"type":"paragraph","content":"LONDON/MOSCOW (Reuters) - Royal Dutch Shell pulled out of a project to build a Russian liquefied natural gas plant partly because Gazprom suddenly added another partner with links to an ally of President Vladimir Putin, according to five sources."},{"type":"primary_image","asset":{"url":"https://static.reuters.com/resources/r/?m=02\u0026d=20190412\u0026t=2\u0026i=1376173661\u0026r=LYNXNPEF3A1S2","caption":"FILE PHOTO: The logo of Gazprom marketing department is seen in front of the office located on the Champs Elysees in Paris ,January 5, 2009. out of a project to build a Russian liquefied natural gas plant partly because Gazprom suddenly added another partner with links to an ally of President Vladimir Putin, according to five sources."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"After three years work on the Baltic Coast project, Shell discovered that Gazprom was bringing in a company linked to Arkady Rotenberg, who is on a U.S. sanctions blacklist."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"The sudden change in the line-up of partners was one of the key factors contributing to Shell’s Wednesday announcement that it was pulling out of the project, according to three sources close to Shell and two other sources familiar with the project."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"Asked to comment on the reasons for withdrawing, a Shell spokesman said it had nothing to add to a previous statement that said its exit followed Gazprom’s announcement last month of its final concept for the project. Gazprom spokesman Sergei Kupriyanov said the company was not commenting."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"According to the two sources close to Shell, Gazprom did not consult with Shell about bringing in the firm, which is called RusGazDobycha, but instead presented it with the plan as a fait accompli."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"With RusGazDobycha’s arrival also came changes to the configuration of the project itself, which Shell did not feel comfortable with, all of the sources said."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"It became untenable for Shell to stay in the project “and that was clear from the moment that Gazprom announced it was going to build the plant together with RusGazDobycha,” said one of the sources familiar with the project."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"A RusGazDobycha official did not respond to a request for comment. Asked if the presidential administration had any role in RusGazDobycha’s entry into the project, Kremlin spokesman Dmitry Peskov said it was a question for the companies involved."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"The sudden shift in the project underlines the unpredictability of doing business in Russia -- even for a firm like Shell with a long pedigree of successful cooperation. It also shows how Rotenberg’s business empire, focused mainly on construction and engineering, is expanding into the energy sector."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"Shell said that its other joint projects in Russia -- chief among them the Gazprom-led Sakhalin-2 LNG plant -- would be unaffected by its exit from the Baltic LNG project."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"But Shell’s involvement in Sakhalin expires this month. Unless the Russian government decides to extend the Sakhalin deal, Shell’s portfolio of Russian projects will be left looking thin."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"The Russian government has given no indication as to whether it would extend Shell’s Sakhalin contract."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"“DIGGING YOUR OWN GRAVE”"},{"type":"paragraph","content":"One of the problems for Shell was that Rotenberg, a long-standing friend of Putin and his former judo training partner, was under sanctions and that created sanctions risks for Shell too, according to one of the sources close to Shell and the second source familiar with the project."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"For Shell, partnering with a Rotenberg-linked firm was tantamount to “digging yourself your own sanctions grave,” said that source."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"But the other sources said the primary issue for Shell was the change in the configuration of the LNG project."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"RusGazDobycha is 100 percent-owned by a firm called National Gas Group (NGG), according to the Spark database, which collates official data from the tax agency and the state statistics agency."},{"type":"paragraph","content":"Until November 2016, Rotenberg had a 51 percent stake in NGG, the database shows.
